Miranda Jr.</a> (father)</li><li>Luz Towns-Miranda (mother)</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Relatives</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miranda_(baseball)" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Miranda (baseball)">Jos\xc3\xa9 Miranda</a> (cousin)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Awards</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Lin-Manuel_Miranda" title="List of awards and nominations received by Lin-Manuel Miranda">Full list</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.linmanuel.com">www<wbr />.linmanuel<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Lin-Manuel Miranda</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;w&#39; in &#39;wind&#39;">w</span><span title="/\xc9\x9b/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">\xc9\x9b</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born January 16, 1980)<sup id="cite_ref-biography.com_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biography.com-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is an American songwriter, <a href="/wiki/Libretto" title="Libretto">librettist</a>, actor, singer, filmmaker, and rapper. He created the Broadway musicals <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Heights" title="In the Heights">In the Heights</a></i> (2005) and <i><a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(musical)" title="Hamilton (musical)">Hamilton</a></i> (2015), and the soundtracks for the animated films <i><a href="/wiki/Moana_(2016_film)" title="Moana (2016 film)">Moana</a></i> (2016), <i><a href="/wiki/Vivo_(film)" title="Vivo (film)">Vivo</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Encanto" title="Encanto">Encanto</a></i> (both 2021). He has received <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Lin-Manuel_Miranda" title="List of awards and nominations received by Lin-Manuel Miranda">numerous accolades</a> including a <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Tony_Awards" title="Tony Awards">Tony Awards</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier_Awards" title="Laurence Olivier Awards">Laurence Olivier Awards</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="Primetime Emmy Awards">Primetime Emmy Awards</a>, and five <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a>, along with nominations for two <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a>. He received the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">Kennedy Center Honors</a> in 2018.\n</p><p>Miranda made his Broadway debut in 2008, writing the music and lyrics for and starring in the musical <i>In the Heights</i>, which won the <a href="/wiki/Tony_Awards" title="Tony Awards">Tony Awards</a> for <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Musical">Best Musical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Tony Award for Best Original Score">Best Original Score</a><sup id="cite_ref-HeightsTony_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HeightsTony-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Musical_Theater_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Musical Theater Album">Grammy Award for Best Musical Theater Album</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HeightGrammy_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HeightGrammy-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was later adapted as a <a href="/wiki/In_the_Heights_(film)" title="In the Heights (film)">2021 film</a> of the same name.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Miranda returned to Broadway in 2015, writing the script, music, and lyrics for as well as starring in the musical <i>Hamilton</i>, which was praised by critics and became a <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">popular culture</a> phenomenon.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i>Hamilton</i> won the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Drama" title="Pulitzer Prize for Drama">Pulitzer Prize for Drama</a> and was nominated for a record 16 <a href="/wiki/Tony_Awards" title="Tony Awards">Tony Awards</a> and won 11, including Miranda\'s first win for the <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Book_of_a_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Book of a Musical">Tony Award for Best Book of a Musical</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(album)" title="Hamilton (album)"><i>Hamilton</i> cast recording</a> spent 10 weeks atop <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <a href="/wiki/Rap_Albums" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap Albums">Top Rap Albums</a> chart and became the eleventh-biggest album of the 2010s.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>A frequent collaborator of <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">the Walt Disney Company</a>, Miranda has written original songs for the studio. He gained two <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Academy Award for Best Original Song</a> nominations for "<a href="/wiki/How_Far_I%27ll_Go" title="How Far I&#39;ll Go">How Far I\'ll Go</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Dos_Oruguitas" title="Dos Oruguitas">Dos Oruguitas</a>" from <i>Moana</i> and <i>Encanto</i>, respectively. The song "<a href="/wiki/We_Don%27t_Talk_About_Bruno" title="We Don&#39;t Talk About Bruno">We Don\'t Talk About Bruno</a>" from <i>Encanto</i> broke various records and marked Miranda\'s first number-one song on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i> Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" class="mw-redirect" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles</a> charts.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He starred as Jack in the musical fantasy <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_Poppins_Returns" title="Mary Poppins Returns">Mary Poppins Returns</a></i> (2018), for which he was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actor_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture_Musical_or_Comedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actor \xe2\x80\x93 Motion Picture Musical or Comedy">Golden Globe Award for Best Actor \xe2\x80\x93 Motion Picture Musical or Comedy</a>. For his performance in the <a href="/wiki/Disney%2B" title="Disney+">Disney+</a> <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(2020_film)" title="Hamilton (2020 film)">live stage recording of <i>Hamilton</i></a> released in 2020, he received a Golden Globe and <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Lead_Actor_in_a_Limited_or_Anthology_Series_or_Movie" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Lead Actor in a Limited or Anthology Series or Movie">Primetime Emmy Award</a> nominations. Miranda debuted as a film director with <i><a href="/wiki/Tick,_Tick..._Boom!_(film)" title="Tick, Tick... Boom! (film)">Tick, Tick...Boom!</a></i> (2021).<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>His television work includes recurring roles on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Electric_Company_(2009_TV_series)" title="The Electric Company (2009 TV series)">The Electric Company</a></i> (2009\xe2\x80\x932010) and <i><a href="/wiki/His_Dark_Materials_(TV_series)" title="His Dark Materials (TV series)">His Dark Materials</a></i> (2019\xe2\x80\x932022). Miranda hosted <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> in 2016 and had a guest role on <i><a href="/wiki/Curb_Your_Enthusiasm" title="Curb Your Enthusiasm">Curb Your Enthusiasm</a></i> in 2018; he was nominated twice for the <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Guest_Actor_in_a_Comedy_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Guest Actor in a Comedy Series">Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Guest Actor in a Comedy Series</a>. He has been politically active on behalf of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pbs11242017_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbs11242017-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Miranda met with politicians in 2016 to speak out in favor of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_government-debt_crisis" title="Puerto Rican government-debt crisis">debt relief for Puerto Rico</a><sup id="cite_ref-pbs11242017_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbs11242017-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and raised funds for rescue efforts and disaster relief after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-wapo5312018_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wapo5312018-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lin-Manuel_Miranda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Miranda was born on January 16, 1980, in New York City to Luz Towns-Miranda, a clinical psychologist, and <a href="/wiki/Luis_A._Miranda_Jr." title="Luis A. Miranda Jr.">Luis Miranda Jr.</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Political_consultant" class="mw-redirect" title="Political consultant">political consultant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-biography.com_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biography.com-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smithsonian_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithsonian-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He is of predominately <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans" title="Puerto Ricans">Puerto Rican</a> descent and also has distant Mexican, English, and African American ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His parents named him "Lin-Manuel" after a poem about the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> by Puerto Rican writer Jos\xc3\xa9 Manuel Torres Santiago entitled "<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Nana roja para mi hijo Lin Manuel</i></span>" ("Red Lullaby for My Son Lin Manuel").<sup id="cite_ref-RebeccaMead_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RebeccaMead-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Miranda grew up in the <a href="/wiki/Inwood,_Manhattan" title="Inwood, Manhattan">Inwood</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> and was raised as a <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-biography.com_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biography.com-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GuardianAncestry_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianAncestry-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During childhood and his teens, Miranda spent at least one month each year with his grandparents in <a href="/wiki/Vega_Alta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Vega Alta, Puerto Rico">Vega Alta</a>, Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-conc_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conc-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Miranda has one older sister, Luz, who is the Chief Financial Officer of the MirRam Group, a strategic consulting firm in Government and Communications.<sup id="cite_ref-thenewyorker_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenewyorker-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Miranda attended <a href="/wiki/Hunter_College_Elementary_School" title="Hunter College Elementary School">Hunter College Elementary School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hunter_College_High_School" title="Hunter College High School">Hunter College High School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Among his classmates was <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hayes" title="Chris Hayes">Chris Hayes</a>, now a journalist. He was Miranda\'s first director when Miranda starred in a school play, described by Hayes as "a 20-minute musical that featured a maniacal fetal pig in a nightmare that [Miranda] had cut up in biology class".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His classmates also included <a href="/wiki/Immortal_Technique" title="Immortal Technique">Immortal Technique</a>, a rapper who had bullied Miranda, although the two later became friends.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Miranda began writing musicals at school.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Miranda wrote the earliest draft of what would become his first Broadway musical, <i>In the Heights,</i> in 1999, during his sophomore year of college at <a href="/wiki/Wesleyan_University" title="Wesleyan University">Wesleyan University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After the show was accepted by Wesleyan\'s student theater company, Second Stage, Miranda added freestyle rap and salsa numbers, and the show was premiered there in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-conc_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conc-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Miranda wrote and directed several other musicals at Wesleyan and acted in many other productions, ranging from musicals to <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>. He graduated from Wesleyan in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-conc_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conc-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYE_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYE-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Career">Career</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lin-Manuel_Miranda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Theatre">Theatre</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lin-Manuel_Miranda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Theatre"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="2002\xe2\x80\x932010:_In_the_Heights"><span id="2002.E2.80.932010:_In_the_Heights"></span>2002\xe2\x80\x932010: <i>In the Heights</i></h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lin-Manuel_Miranda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2002\xe2\x80\x932010: In the Heights"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/In_the_Heights" title="In the Heights">In the Heights</a></div>\n<p>In 2002, Miranda and <a href="/wiki/John_Buffalo_Mailer" title="John Buffalo Mailer">John Buffalo Mailer</a> worked with director <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Kail" title="Thomas Kail">Thomas Kail</a> to revise <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Heights" title="In the Heights">In the Heights</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-conc_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conc-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smithsonian_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithsonian-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Playwright <a href="/wiki/Quiara_Alegr%C3%ADa_Hudes" title="Quiara Alegr\xc3\xada Hudes">Quiara Alegr\xc3\xada Hudes</a> joined the team in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After premiering in Connecticut in 2005 and opening at the 37 Arts Theater <a href="/wiki/Off-Broadway" title="Off-Broadway">off-Broadway</a> in 2007, the musical went to <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a>, opening in March 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-conc_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conc-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>It was nominated for 13 <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Tony Award">Tony Awards</a>, winning four, including <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Musical">Best Musical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Tony Award for Best Original Score">Best Original Score</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HeightsTony_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HeightsTony-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Musical_Theater_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Musical Theater Album">Grammy Award for Best Musical Theater Album</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HeightGrammy_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HeightGrammy-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Miranda\'s performance in the leading role of Usnavi earned him a nomination for the <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Actor_in_a_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Actor in a Musical">Tony Award for Best Actor in a Musical</a>. Miranda left the cast of the Broadway production on February 15, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Miranda reprised the role when the national tour of <i>In the Heights</i> played in Los Angeles from June 23 to July 25, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He again joined the tour in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Miranda rejoined the Broadway cast as Usnavi from December 25, 2010, until the production closed on January 9, 2011, after 29 previews and 1,185 regular performances.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Miranda created other work for the stage during this period. He wrote Spanish-language dialogue and worked with <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Sondheim" title="Stephen Sondheim">Stephen Sondheim</a> to translate into Spanish song lyrics for the 2009 Broadway revival of <i><a href="/wiki/West_Side_Story" title="West Side Story">West Side Story</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_29-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During this time, he also performed at bar and bat mitzvahs.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_29-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2008, he was invited by composer-lyricist <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Schwartz_(composer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Schwartz (composer)">Stephen Schwartz</a> to contribute two new songs to a revised version of Schwartz and Nina Faso\'s 1978 musical <i><a href="/wiki/Working_(musical)" title="Working (musical)">Working</a></i>, which opened in May 2008 at the <a href="/wiki/Asolo_Repertory_Theatre" title="Asolo Repertory Theatre">Asolo Repertory Theatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sarasota,_Florida" title="Sarasota, Florida">Sarasota, Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>During these years, Miranda worked as an English teacher at his former high school, wrote for the <i><a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Times" title="Manhattan Times">Manhattan Times</a></i> as a columnist and <a href="/wiki/Restaurant_critic" class="mw-redirect" title="Restaurant critic">restaurant critic</a>, and composed music for commercials.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2003, Miranda co-founded <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_Love_Supreme" title="Freestyle Love Supreme">Freestyle Love Supreme</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> a hip hop improv group that has toured the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Festival_Fringe" title="Edinburgh Festival Fringe">Edinburgh Festival Fringe</a>, as well as the Aspen, Melbourne and Montreal Comedy festivals. The group created a limited television series for Pivot in 2014<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and made its Broadway debut<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> on October 2, 2019, at the <a href="/wiki/Booth_Theatre" title="Booth Theatre">Booth Theatre</a>. The self-titled show gained positive reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="2011\xe2\x80\x932014:_Bring_It_On_and_other_theatrical_work"><span id="2011.E2.80.932014:_Bring_It_On_and_other_theatrical_work"></span>2011\xe2\x80\x932014: <i>Bring It On</i> and other theatrical work</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lin-Manuel_Miranda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2011\xe2\x80\x932014: Bring It On and other theatrical work"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bring_It_On:_The_Musical" title="Bring It On: The Musical">Bring It On: The Musical</a></div>\n<p>Miranda co-wrote the music and lyrics for <i><a href="/wiki/Bring_It_On:_The_Musical" title="Bring It On: The Musical">Bring It On: The Musical</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Tom_Kitt_(musician)" title="Tom Kitt (musician)">Tom Kitt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Green" title="Amanda Green">Amanda Green</a>. <i>Bring It On</i> premiered at the Alliance Theatre in Atlanta, Georgia in January 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The musical began a US national tour on October 30, 2011, in Los Angeles, California.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It played a limited engagement on Broadway at the <a href="/wiki/St._James_Theatre" title="St. James Theatre">St. James Theatre</a>, beginning previews on July 12, and officially opening on August 1, 2012. It closed on December 30, 2012. It was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Tony_Awards" title="Tony Awards">Tony Awards</a> in the categories of Best Musical and Best Choreography.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2012, Miranda appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Merrily_We_Roll_Along_(musical)" title="Merrily We Roll Along (musical)">Merrily We Roll Along</a></i>, in the role of Charley, in an <i><a href="/wiki/Encores!" title="Encores!">Encores!</a></i> staged concert at <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Center" title="New York City Center">New York City Center</a>.\n</p><p>His theatrical achievements in 2014 included an <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> for the song "Bigger!", which he and Kitt co-wrote for the opening number at the <a href="/wiki/67th_Tony_Awards" title="67th Tony Awards">67th Tony Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Miranda wrote music and lyrics for the one-act musical <i><a href="/wiki/21_Chump_Street" title="21 Chump Street">21 Chump Street</a></i>, and performed as narrator for the show\'s single performance at the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Academy_of_Music" title="Brooklyn Academy of Music">Brooklyn Academy of Music</a> on June 7, 2014. It was broadcast on <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" class="mw-redirect" title="National Public Radio">National Public Radio</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/This_American_Life" title="This American Life">This American Life</a></i> on June 20, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later that month, he starred in the June 2014 <i>Encores!</i> revival of <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Larson" title="Jonathan Larson">Jonathan Larson</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Tick,_Tick..._Boom!" title="Tick, Tick... Boom!">Tick, Tick... Boom!</a></i>, under the artistic direction of <a href="/wiki/Jeanine_Tesori" title="Jeanine Tesori">Jeanine Tesori</a>. The show was directed by <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Butler" class="mw-redirect" title="Oliver Butler">Oliver Butler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Earlier in 2014, he guest starred in a show by comedy duo <a href="/wiki/The_Skivvies" title="The Skivvies">The Skivvies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="2011\xe2\x80\x932016:_Hamilton"><span id="2011.E2.80.932016:_Hamilton"></span>2011\xe2\x80\x932016: <i>Hamilton</i></h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lin-Manuel_Miranda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2011\xe2\x80\x932016: Hamilton"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(musical)" title="Hamilton (musical)">Hamilton (musical)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(2020_film)" title="Hamilton (2020 film)">Hamilton (2020 film)</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lin-Manuel_Miranda_in_Hamilton.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lin-Manuel_Miranda_in_Hamilton.jpg/220px-Lin-Manuel_Miranda_in_Hamilton.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="171" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lin-Manuel_Miranda_in_Hamilton.jpg/330px-Lin-Manuel_Miranda_in_Hamilton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lin-Manuel_Miranda_in_Hamilton.jpg/440px-Lin-Manuel_Miranda_in_Hamilton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3013" data-file-height="2345" /></a><figcaption>Miranda in <i>Hamilton</i>, 2016</figcaption></figure>\n<p>While on vacation in 2008, Lin-Manuel Miranda had read <a href="/wiki/Ron_Chernow" title="Ron Chernow">Ron Chernow</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton_(book)" title="Alexander Hamilton (book)">biography</a> of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">Alexander Hamilton</a>. Inspired by the book, he wrote a rap about Hamilton that he performed for the White House Evening of Poetry, Music, and the Spoken Word on May 12, 2009, accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Alex_Lacamoire" title="Alex Lacamoire">Alex Lacamoire</a>. Miranda later said he spent a year writing the <i>Hamilton</i> song "<a href="/wiki/My_Shot" title="My Shot">My Shot</a>", revising it countless times so that every verse would reflect Alexander Hamilton\'s intellect.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RebeccaMead_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RebeccaMead-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By 2012, Miranda was performing an extended set of pieces based on the life of Hamilton, which he referred to as the <i>Hamilton Mixtape.</i> <i>The New York Times</i> called it "an obvious game changer".<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(musical)" title="Hamilton (musical)">Hamilton: An American Musical</a></i> premiered off-Broadway at <a href="/wiki/The_Public_Theater" title="The Public Theater">The Public Theater</a> in January 2015, directed by Thomas Kail. Miranda wrote the book and score and starred as the title character.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The show received highly positive reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and its engagement was sold out.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Chernow and Miranda received the 2015 History Makers Award from the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Historical_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Historical Society">New York Historical Society</a> for their work in creating the musical.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The show began previews on Broadway in July 2015 at the <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rodgers_Theatre" title="Richard Rodgers Theatre">Richard Rodgers Theatre</a> and officially opened on August 6, 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> earning positive reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On the first night of <i>Hamilton</i> previews, over 700 people lined up for lottery tickets.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <i>Hamilton</i> ticket lottery evolved into <a href="/wiki/Ham4Ham" class="mw-redirect" title="Ham4Ham">Ham4Ham</a>, a series of outdoor mini-performances for lottery participants that was hosted daily by Miranda and cast members for over a year, until August 31, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Miranda earned a 3% royalty on each performance of <i>Hamilton</i>, earning him $12.7&#160;million by July 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i>Hamilton</i> won the <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Musical">Tony Award for Best Musical</a>; Miranda won Tony Awards for <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Tony Award for Best Original Score">Best Original Score</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Book_of_a_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Book of a Musical">Best Book of a Musical</a> and was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Actor_in_a_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Actor in a Musical">Best Actor in a Musical</a>. Miranda won the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Drama" title="Pulitzer Prize for Drama">Pulitzer Prize for Drama</a> for the musical, and the <i>Hamilton</i> cast album won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Musical_Theater_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Musical Theater Album">Grammy Award for Best Musical Theater Album</a>. In May 2016, for his work in the role of Alexander Hamilton, Miranda received the <a href="/wiki/Drama_League_Award" title="Drama League Award">Drama League</a> <a href="/wiki/Drama_League_Distinguished_Performance_Award" title="Drama League Distinguished Performance Award">Distinguished Performance Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><video id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Rose_Garden_Freestyle_feat._Lin-Manuel_Miranda.webm/250px--Rose_Garden_Freestyle_feat._Lin-Manuel_Miranda.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" data-mw-tmh="" class="mw-file-element" width="250" height="141" data-durationhint="103" data-mwtitle="Rose_Garden_Freestyle_feat._Lin-Manuel_Miranda.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:Rose_Garden_Freestyle_feat._Lin-Manuel_Miranda.webm"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/f4/Rose_Garden_Freestyle_feat._Lin-Manuel_Miranda.webm/Rose_Garden_Freestyle_feat._Lin-Manuel_Miranda.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-transcodekey="720p.vp9.webm" data-width="1280" data-height="720" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Rose_Garden_Freestyle_feat._Lin-Manuel_Miranda.webm" type="video/webm;
